B0012E6R3W|5.0|Anybody that knows heavy metal music already knows the story behind Testament's \\"The Formation Of Damnation.\\" It is the group's ninth studio recording, but their first since \\"The Gathering\\" was released all the way back in 1999. It is also their first record of completely new material to feature original axe virtuoso Alex Skolnick and bassist Greg Christian since Testament's \\"Low\\" came out five years prior to the above-named release (in 1994).<br /><br />So that much is obvious. But what you might not have known is that \\"The Formation...\\" is a not just a spectacular comeback album, it is a spectacular album period. Easily one of the best \\"true blue\\" thrash releases of the new millennium, this fine effort is filled with great riffs and even greater solos. As such, metalheads everywhere should be found drooling when listening to \\"The Formation,\\" and agree with the fact  that it is a highly contagious and instantly memorable affair, and one that easily ranks alongside the group's all-time best material.<br /><br />The album begins with \\"For The Glory Of...,\\" an instrumental introductory piece that is thoroughly thunderous, except for its use of nifty melodic guitar leads near its end. Next comes \\"More Than Meets The Eye,\\"which,with its catchy gallop, fiery, chugging licks, steady, staccato bass lines, and rhythmically martial drum beat, just might be mistaken by some fans for being an Iron Maiden b-side if not for only frontman Chuck  Billy's visceral, and near death metal-worthy growls. And the song is also further  highlighted by a blistering melodic solo section, and a catchy  vocal refrain. (It is darn near impossible not to sing-along to its\\"ooh\\" and \\"woah\\" bits.) \\"The Evil Has Landed\\"sounds similar, augmenting a wealth of strong, crunching riffs with a soaring, wailing, and epically  twiddly guitar solo that rips the air like a serrated knife. The title track, then, stands out for quite possibly being \\"Formation\\"'s heaviest number. Its thunderous, pounding rhythms, blistering, machine-gun fast picking, and tight and precise double kick drumming attest to that. Another ripping, harmonic guitar solo is also included, here, as is a bunch of strong, bobbing hooks (produced by a galloping beat that interlocks with staccato guitar leads). And \\"Formation\\" (the song) also features a lengthy,strung-out,yet decisively non-hardcore mid-song breakdown.<br /><br />\\"Dangers Of TheFaithless\\" marries some catchy, \\"Enter Sandman\\"-era Metallica-reminiscent chugging with a hooky, Anthrax-style call-and-response shout and a funky-sounding bass line that snakes its way through the arrangements. And it is all capped off by the record's best guitar solo -- and what an amazing solo it is, too! It is of the epically epic, dive-bombing, and shred-happy variety, thus making it fifty-plus seconds in length. Although not quite as irresisitble as the above, the subsequent \\"The Persecuted Won't Forget\\" is another big standout track in that it allows Testament to really flex their brutal, old-school thrash muscle. Indeed, aside from some nice, Maiden-ish harmonies and pair of melodic solos around the song's mid-section (which are necessary in order to break up the  tune's monotony), this is one scorching, and very breakneck speedster from beginning to end. \\"Henchmen Ride,\\" then, continues in this same vein, as it is an Eighties-era thrasher that finds the guitarists continuing to crunch away at blazing speeds. (And it kicks off with a small-ish, but  nevertheless impressive  drum intro, too.)<br /><br />Next up, \\"Killing Season\\" might feature some more really memorable vocal patterns and instinctively infectious choruses. But again, it is the guitarists -- Skolnick and Eric Peterson -- that mainly run the show, here, by uncorking some big, fat, juicy riffs and positively air-guitar-able melodic soloing throughout. Then, following the hefty chug and churner that is \\"Afterlife,\\" comes \\"F.E.A.R.,\\" which overflows with more blistering thrash picking and surprisingly fast and brutal double bass blasts. Another excellent solo is included here,too, and so are some mid-tempo (and, again, non-hardcore), chugging breakdowns that, together with the inclusion of sing-songy vocals (and a catchy,shouted refrain of \\"Fear! Fear!\\"), make the track's choruses truly unforgettable and epic. The album then concludes with \\"Leave Me Forever,\\" a thoroughly mid-tempo and brooding number with an ominous, grumbling bass line.<br /><br />The bottom line here is that it maybe should not have taken nine years to make, but \\"Formation Of Damnation\\" is nonetheless an excellent album. It easily ranks amongst the top twenty metal albums released in 2008,and is also very likely the year's best comeback record. It might be said year's finest piece of pure/traditional/old-fashioned thrash metal, but it sure comes close to being that. (It does not usurp Metallica's \\"Death Magnetic\\" for being the winner of  that category; but, then again, no album does.)isingly fast and brutal double bass blasts. B0085RQLXK|4.0|With Aerosmith frontman Steven Tyler moonlighting as a celebrity guest host (Simon Cowell's replacement) on you know which American reality show, and the band having not released an album of entirely new material in the better part of a decade, many music fans probably forgot about Aerosmith, or at least thought that they had run their course (and understandably so, too). But once Tyler bailed on the T.V. show, cries of \\"sell-out!\\" dimmed as the Blue Army immediately forgave him and looked forward to a new album and at least one tour from their favorite hard rock group.<br /><br />Poised to take the world by storm with one heckuva comeback, Tyler and the gang did just that with \\"Music From Another Dimension,\\" their first new studio record in over eight years. And this effort might not be quite what you were hoping for it to be, but hey, when an album undergoes as much pre-release hype as this one did, it is almost impossible to expect it to live up to it. But what \\"Music\\" DOES do, however, is feature all of the characteristics that the band has relied on since the early Seventies. Like saucy, sleazy guitar licks, exceptional solos, Tyler's trademark wail, fat bass, workmanlike drumming, and offensive lyricism. Hence, it is definitely a release that is all-but sure to please and satisfy all of Aerosmith's hungry fanbase.<br /><br /> \\"LUV XXX\\" is an insanely catchy album opener with a funky, hard-rockin' main guitar lick and some insanely hooky and memorable vocal patterns. And the song is further highlighted by a batch of good guitar soloing that is tacked on into the mix near the end. Next up comes the very, very Rolling Stones-esque rocker, \\"Oh Yeah,\\" which has some really catchy vocal patterns (including some wailing female backing vocals), a bluesy, and even borderline wailing solo, and some jazzy-sounding brass horn flourishes. Then, following the mostly unremarkable and forgettable \\"Beautiful\\" comes \\"Tell Me,\\" a bluegrass-flavored acoustic strummer with dramatic drum fills and Steven Tyler's wailing, upper-register vocals. A catchy, staccato guitar riff introduces the next song after that, \\"Out Go The Lights,\\" which leads the way, and flows into a cowbell-tinged groove, before uncorking a good, shredding guitar solo. Some more female vocals pepper the arrangements, as does some wailing harmonica soloing. And this number, while admittedly a bit on the overlong side, is a mightily catchy one, as it overflows with terrific hooks of all kinds.<br /><br />\\"Legendary Child\\" is one of the set's biggest highlights, as it sounds almost as if it could have been lifted wholesale off of a Led Zeppelin recording, except for the fact that it has some Ozzy Osbourne-influenced singing. Of the eight songs that remain, three are ballads. \\"What Could Have Been Love\\" is a lovely and soaring acoustic ditty; \\"Can't Stop Lovin' You\\" might have an AC-DC-esque song title, but it is, in actuality, a southern rock-flavored duet with Carrie Underwood (the season four winner of \\"American Idol\\"); and \\"We All Fall Down\\" is a placid, piano-based number with soulful vocals. These three ballads are almost overshadowed, however, by tracks like \\"Street Jesus,\\" which is the album's epic centerpiece that clocks in at six-plus minutes in length. It is a surprisingly up-tempo piece that rocks harder than anything else on the record, and features a tasty, pyrotechnic-esque trade-off guitar solo section.<br /><br />And there is another handful of noteworthy mentions that round out the rest of the album. Track ten, \\"Lover A lot,\\" finds the aforementioned Led Zeppelin influence coming back as strong as ever, and boasts a John Bonham-approved drum intro followed by plenty of pronounced, dirty/grungy-sounding bass grumbles, and really catchy and addictive choruses. \\"Freedom Fighter\\" (which has guest backing vocals from Johnny Depp, of all people) is another feel-good, up-tempo rocker peppered with some jazzy, Jerry Lee Lewis-styled piano breaks. And, finally, there is \\"Something,\\" which has colorful slide guitar and organ runs amplified by some of Tom Hamilton's best, heaviest, and meatiest bass lines. It also boasts guest percussion work from the aforementioned frontman (Tyler).<br /><br />\\"Music From Another Dimension\\" comes up short of being 2012's best comeback album, and it isn't the year's best pure hard rock recording, either. (It ranks second in both of those categories to Soundgarden's \\"King Animal.\\") And plus, \\"Music\\" is not quite as heavy as this reviewer would have liked it to have been. But if any of this sounds like I am dissing on this album, I'm actually not. After all, it is irrefutable proof of the fact that If you like your hard rock raucous-yet-simultaneously-tuneful, rock-ready, energetic, infectiously hooky, meticulously well-crafted, and professionally played, it would be a huge mistake to write off and/or forget about Aerosmith just yet.s \\"Something,\\" which has colorful slide guitar and organ runs amplified by some of Tom Hamilton's best, heaviest, and meatiest bass lines. B0067EKYS6|4.0|I finally got to see the new \\"The Great Gatsby\\" movie and was surprised at how good it was. I was expecting it to be awful given my opinion of director Baz Luhrmann's prior work, notably the insipid \\"[[ASIN:B000077VR3 Moulin Rouge!]]\\"<br /><br />Although there were considerable liberties and abridgements taken with the story, the core of it was definitely preserved and, more importantly, the contradictory but simultaneously elegaic and exuberant tone of the novel was preserved.<br /><br />Earlier adaptations, such as the [[ASIN:B00AEFY66U 1974 version with Robert Redford]], were so plodding as to be almost unwatchable. The 1974 movie makes the fatal mistake of being too realistic, reducing the whole affair to something like a Lifeiime television movie. That's exactly what you get from the novel if you distill the bare plot and characters but lose the tone, because the novel is ultimately structured as a nostalgic remembrance of lost hope. The deliberately unrealistic excitement of a period in time when anything seemed possible is the perfect environment for Baz Luhrmann.<br /><br />In the new version, the cinematography and costumes mesh well to convey the excitement of the Jazz Age at its peak.<br /><br />The music was surprisingly appropriate, the exact opposite of \\"Moulin Rouge,\\" with George Gershwin's \\"Rhapsody in Blue\\" -- one of my all-time favorite pieces -- as a significant recurring motif. Even the new music, especially \\"Young and Beautiful,\\" fits in well.<br /><br />The movie is visually very impressive in a way that the novel cannot be, but it does conjure an imaginary and unrealistic world of grandiose excess that is worth seeing. The 3D gimmick is kind of pointless, but that is true for most movies.<br /><br />Without spoiling anything, the opening credits begin in rough black and white with uneven lighting and flicker, very much like watching an old movie actually made in the 1920s, before the credits change to sharp and colorful gilded art deco designs. The effect is clever, making all of the flashy color that is the movie seem almost dreamlike, copying the elegaic tone of the novel. Eventually the closing credits reverse the effect back to fuzzy black and white.<br /><br />Gatsby is an archetypal character whose purity and single-mindedness are his defining elements, creating a kind of naivety that distinguishes him from everyone around him -- and which eventually destroys him at the hands of those more cynical. One of the main reasons why the novel has become what it is today is that it presciently in 1925 understood that the Roaring 20s were an unsustainable party that must come to an end, which we know now from hindsight would happen with a horrific crash and decade-long hangover of the Great Depression. F. Scott Fitzgerald's almost puritanical discomfort with the Jazz Age, despite being its most enthusiastic contemporaneous chronicler, proved to strike just the right chord. A very good book about the 1920s Paris expatriate community (of which Scott and Zelda were prominent members) borrows a quote from a less well known writer as its title: \\"[[ASIN:0767903706 Everybody Was So Young]].\\"<br /><br />The characters are all very dislikable, with the exception of Jay Gatsby himself. Nick Carraway is extremely self-critical, regarding himself as a failure. One of the most common criticisms of the novel is that Gatsby's interest in Daisy lacks credibility because she is something of a petulant child who needs to be taken care of, but of course she mirrors to some extent Scott's real-life wife Zelda and their co-dependent marriage. Regardless of the truth about Zelda, who was by all accounts a remarkably capable and intelligent woman, there can be no doubt that she was treated as someone who needed to be taken care of and eventually ended up confined to a mental hospital. I don't want to fall into the trap of misidentifying authors with their characters, but it seems clear that Scott intended Gatsby's interest is Daisy to be entirely credible, even if Gatsby's perception of her was idealized as a result of his naivety and boundless optimism.<br /><br />The original novel is unstinting in its portrayal of the mistreatment of servants, which is intended to be offensive. What Scott Fitzgerald fully intended to condemn in 1925 looks even worse to us now, but it is an important part of the story and is an essential literary device used repeatedly to illuminate the defects of Tom Buchanan's character and worldview. The novel draws explicit parallels between Gatsby, as what would then be disparaged as a \\"self-made man,\\" and the servants --- both of whom Tom believes are limited and inexorably predestined by their circumstances of birth. Indeed, one of the reasons Tom is so disgusted at being described as \\"the polo player\\" is because being known for what he does instead of how he was born degrades him, in his own view, to the level of competition with Gatsby and the servants.<br /><br />I should explain somewhat my comment about \\"liberties and abridgements.\\" There are a number of lines of narration and dialogue that, although quite widely known and remembered from the novel, are simply gone in the movie. The opening and closing text is preserved, as it had to be, but everything else was apparently up for challenge about inclusion.<br /><br />Almost all of the subplots are removed, which reduces some of the characters to very minor status, especially Jordan Baker who in the novel is an iconic representation of the independent \\"new woman\\" that we might today call a \\"feminist,\\" and is therefore a counterpart to narrator Nick Carraway who, although of respectable pedigree and a Yale alumnus, has to actually work for a living. The screenwriters were probably correct in thinking that this was of much less interest to the modern audience than it was when the novel was published. On the other hand, it makes some things incomprehensible, such as why Tom Buchanan gets so annoyed at being introduced as \\"the polo player.\\"<br /><br />The handling of the Meyer Wolfsheim character is outright bizarre, probably because there were fears of the portrayal being regarded as anti-Semitic despite the character unquestionably being based on the real-life Arnold Rothstein. For one thing, he is played by an actor whose ancestry is from India, a pretty extreme case of \\"funny, he doesn't look Jewish,\\" and who is the only actor who seems to have any identifiable ethnicity with a speaking role that is not a black waiter. Odd things are changed, such as his cufflinks made from human teeth turning into a tie-pin, possibly because the screenwriters were worried that the modern audience would be too confused as to what cufflinks are, but the cufflinks are significant because they are something that would not be noticed immediately but when noticed would pierce the veneer of civility -- a major theme in the novel.<br /><br />It's a vibrant, colorful movie that successfully evokes, if not the real Jazz Age, then our collective historical memory of it.

B00BLSJI80|3.0|Demi Lovato attempts to make the transition from being exclusively a teen-pop artist to being an artist who can straddle both adults and younger audiences.  Thoughout 2013's [[ASIN:B00BLSJI80 Demi]], Lovato often executes this balance well, making the effort an overall enjoyable one to listen to. Even so, Demi has its flaws at times, be it over-singing on Lovato's part, one too any ballads, or somewhat generic, indistinct songwriting.  The good news is that the 13-track affair has no gargantuan flubs and suits Lovato's purpose and highlights her continually growing pipes and artistry.<br /><br />Two 'home runs' establish Demi from the get-go. \\"Heart Attack\\" is catchy and well produced, finding Lovato infusing plenty of personality.  The modern pop cues that characterize music of the day are well at work with \\"Heart Attack\\" benefitting greatly from this conformity.  On \\"Made in the USA\\" she doesn't let down, commanding impressively with her big, 20 year old pipes. \\"No matter how far we go, I want the whole world to know / I want you, and I won't have it any other way / no matter that we'll never break / cause our love was made, made in the USA...\\", Lovato sings enthusiastically on the chorus. The follow up to the album's chief juggernauts, \\"Without the Love\\" isn't too shabby, making nice use of acoustic guitars and strings within the production work. Lovato shines particularly on the bridge and generally throughout on her ad libs.<br /><br />\\"Neon Lights\\" is Lovato's dance-pop moment, contrasting the previous trio of cuts. The main rub is that \\"Neon Lights\\" sounds much like a host of similar sounding, generic danceable cuts. Lovato screams a bit on the peak of the chorus, showing her trying a bit too hard.  On \\"Two Pieces\\", the song literally has two different pieces fused together. The verse has more of a folksy, singer/songwriter vibe in six-eight time, while the chorus switches back to standard common time with an anthemic nature.  Ultimately, \\"Two Pieces\\" serves as a welcome contrast to \\"Neon Lights\\", but doesn't eclipse \\"Heart Attack\\" nor \\"Made in the USA\\". Continuing with balladry, Lovato has two nice moments with \\"Nightingale\\" and \\"In Case\\". Sometimes she grows overexcited (\\"Nightingale\\"), but it's hard to knock her effort. \\"In Case\\", an exposed, stripped cut, gives off an Adele \\"Someone Like You\\" vibe. It's not the same caliber mind you, but shows Lovato's potential if nothing else.<br /><br />\\"Really Don't Care\\" (featuring Cher Lloyd) arrives timely to propel the tempo after three consecutive slower cuts.  Peppy and definitely suited to Lovato's core base, \\"Really Don't Care\\" may be schmaltzy, but it is one of the best of the album.  \\"Fire Starter\\" benefits from keeping the tempo up, but feels as if it is missing an extra 'spark'. Sure she excites as she proclaims \\"I'm a fire starter / make your blood run faster / I melt hearts like water...\\", but the cut lacks the same amount of fun of \\"Really Don't Care\\". The teen-poppy \\"Something That We're Not\\" is arguably more fun while \\"Never Been Hurt\\" takes a back step with a few vocal imperfections (during a gimmicky tag at the end of the chorus).  \\"Shouldn't Come Back\\" pulls back the tempo.  A bit boring, the cut grows and excites after a so-so start.  Closing cut \\"Warrior\\" is a powerful ballad.  The main rub? Having back to back ballads to close the effort may be excessive.<br /><br />Ultimately, [[ASIN:B00BLSJI80 Demi]] is a solid effort, not a perfect one. To her fan base, four and five star reviews will likely flood in, particularly those who have followed her career closely. But to the more casual pop listener, this is 'good' but not 'show-stopping'. No one will deny Lovato's potential; it is quite high. 3 stars.as a welcome contrast to \\"Neon Lights\\", but doesn't eclipse \\"Heart Attack\\" nor \\"Made in the USA\\".
